<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Luxembourg">Luxembourg</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reformation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Luxembourg">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Protestantism_in_Luxembourg" title="Protestantism in Luxembourg">Protestantism in Luxembourg</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Luxembourg" title="Luxembourg">Luxembourg</a>, a part of the Spanish Netherlands, remained Catholic during the Reformation era because Protestantism was illegal until 1768.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Hungary">Hungary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reformation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Hungary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Reformation_in_the_Kingdom_of_Hungary" title="Reformation in the Kingdom of Hungary">Reformation in the Kingdom of Hungary</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:4k_ref_portre_bocskai.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1533" data-file-width="1242" decoding="async" height="210" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/4k_ref_portre_bocskai.jpg/170px-4k_ref_portre_bocskai.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/4k_ref_portre_bocskai.jpg/255px-4k_ref_portre_bocskai.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/4k_ref_portre_bocskai.jpg/340px-4k_ref_portre_bocskai.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:4k_ref_portre_bocskai.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stephen_Bocskay" title="Stephen Bocskay">Stephen Bocskay</a> prevented the Holy Roman Emperor from imposing Catholicism on Hungarians.</div></div></div>
<p>Much of the population of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hungary" title="Kingdom of Hungary">Kingdom of Hungary</a> adopted Protestantism during the 16th century. After the 1526 <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Moh%C3%A1cs" title="Battle of Mohács">Battle of Mohács</a>, the Hungarian people were disillusioned by the inability of the government to protect them and turned to the faith they felt would infuse them with the strength necessary to resist the invader. They found this in the teaching of Protestant reformers such as <a href="/wiki/Martin_Luther" title="Martin Luther">Martin Luther</a>. The spread of Protestantism in the country was assisted by its large ethnic German minority, which could understand and translate the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Martin_Luther_(resources)" title="Martin Luther (resources)">writings of Martin Luther</a>. While <a href="/wiki/Lutheranism" title="Lutheranism">Lutheranism</a> gained a foothold among the German- and Slovak-speaking populations, <a href="/wiki/Calvinism" title="Calvinism">Calvinism</a> became widely accepted among ethnic Hungarians.
</p><p>In the more independent northwest, the rulers and priests, protected now by the <a href="/wiki/Habsburg_monarchy" title="Habsburg monarchy">Habsburg monarchy</a>, which had taken the field to fight the Turks, defended the old Catholic faith. They dragged the Protestants to prison and the stake wherever they could. Such strong measures only fanned the flames of protest, however. Leaders of the Protestants included <a href="/wiki/Matthias_D%C3%A9vay" title="Matthias Dévay">Mátyás Dévai Bíró</a>, Mihály Sztárai, István Szegedi Kis, and <a href="/wiki/Ferenc_D%C3%A1vid" title="Ferenc Dávid">Ferenc Dávid</a>.
</p><p>Protestants likely formed a majority of Hungary's population at the close of the 16th century, but <a href="/wiki/Counter-Reformation" title="Counter-Reformation">Counter-Reformation</a> efforts in the 17th century reconverted a majority of the kingdom to Catholicism. A significant Protestant minority remained, most of it adhering to the Calvinist faith.
</p><p>In 1558 the <a href="/wiki/Transylvania" title="Transylvania">Transylvanian</a> <a href="/wiki/Diet_(assembly)" title="Diet (assembly)">Diet</a> of <a href="/wiki/Turda" title="Turda">Turda</a> decreed the free practice of both the Catholic and Lutheran religions, but prohibited <a href="/wiki/Calvinism" title="Calvinism">Calvinism</a>. Ten years later, in 1568, the Diet extended this freedom, declaring that "It is not allowed to anybody to intimidate anybody with captivity or expulsion for his religion". Four religions were declared to be "accepted" (<i>recepta</i>) religions (the fourth being <a href="/wiki/Unitarianism" title="Unitarianism">Unitarianism</a>, which became official in 1583 as the faith of the only Unitarian king, <a href="/wiki/John_Sigismund_Z%C3%A1polya" title="John Sigismund Zápolya">John II Sigismund Zápolya</a>, r. 1540–1571), while <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Eastern Orthodox Christianity</a> was "tolerated" (though the building of stone Orthodox churches was forbidden). During the <a href="/wiki/Thirty_Years%27_War" title="Thirty Years' War">Thirty Years' War</a>, Royal (Habsburg) Hungary joined the Catholic side, until Transylvania joined the Protestant side.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>Between 1604 and 1711, there was a series of anti-Habsburg uprisings calling for equal rights and freedom for all Christian denominations, with varying success; the uprisings were usually organised from Transylvania. The Habsburg-sanctioned Counter-Reformation efforts in the 17th century reconverted the majority of the kingdom to Catholicism.
</p><p>The center of Protestant learning in Hungary has for some centuries been the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Debrecen" title="University of Debrecen">University of Debrecen</a>. Founded in 1538, the university was situated in an area of Eastern Hungary under Ottoman Turkish rule during the 1600s and 1700s, being allowed Islamic toleration and thus avoiding Counter-Reformation persecution.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Romania">Romania</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reformation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Romania">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Dimitrije_Ljubavi%C4%87#Reformation:_Lutherans_and_Serbs" title="Dimitrije Ljubavić">Dimitrije Ljubavić § Reformation: Lutherans and Serbs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Romania#Protestantism" title="Religion in Romania">Religion in Romania § Protestantism</a>, and <a href="/wiki/History_of_Christianity_in_Romania#Reformation" title="History of Christianity in Romania">History of Christianity in Romania § Reformation</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Transylvania" title="Transylvania">Transylvania</a> in what is today's <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a> was a "dumping ground for undesirables" by the <a href="/wiki/Habsburg_monarchy" title="Habsburg monarchy">Habsburg monarchy</a>. People who did not conform to the will of the Habsburgs and the leaders of the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic Church</a> were forcibly sent there. Centuries of this practice allowed diverse Protestant traditions to emerge in Romania, including <a href="/wiki/Lutheranism" title="Lutheranism">Lutheranism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Calvinism" title="Calvinism">Calvinism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Unitarianism" title="Unitarianism">Unitarianism</a>.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Ukraine">Ukraine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reformation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Ukraine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Protestantism_in_Ukraine" title="Protestantism in Ukraine">Protestantism in Ukraine</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Calvinism" title="Calvinism">Calvinism</a> was popular among <a href="/wiki/Hungarians" title="Hungarians">Hungarians</a> who inhabited the southwestern parts of the present-day Ukraine. Their descendants are still there, such as the <a href="/wiki/Sub-Carpathian_Reformed_Church" title="Sub-Carpathian Reformed Church">Sub-Carpathian Reformed Church</a>.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Belarus">Belarus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reformation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Belarus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Reformation#Polish–Lithuanian_Commonwealth" title="Reformation">Reformation § Polish–Lithuanian_Commonwealth</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reformation_in_Poland" title="Reformation in Poland">Reformation in Poland</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Counter-Reformation_in_Poland" title="Counter-Reformation in Poland">Counter-Reformation in Poland</a></div>
<p>The first Protestant congregation was founded in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brest-Litovsk" title="Brest-Litovsk">Brest-Litovsk</a> in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reformed_tradition" title="Reformed tradition">Reformed tradition</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Belarusian_Evangelical_Reformed_Church" title="Belarusian Evangelical Reformed Church">Belarusian Evangelical Reformed Church</a> exists today.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Ireland">Ireland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reformation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Ireland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Reformation_in_Ireland" title="Reformation in Ireland">Reformation in Ireland</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Anthonis_Mor_001.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1894" data-file-width="1426" decoding="async" height="226" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Anthonis_Mor_001.jpg/170px-Anthonis_Mor_001.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Anthonis_Mor_001.jpg/255px-Anthonis_Mor_001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Anthonis_Mor_001.jpg/340px-Anthonis_Mor_001.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Anthonis_Mor_001.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A devout Catholic, <a href="/wiki/Mary_I_of_England" title="Mary I of England">Mary I of England</a> started the first <a href="/wiki/Plantations_of_Ireland" title="Plantations of Ireland">Plantations of Ireland</a>, which, ironically, soon came to be associated with Protestantism.</div></div></div>
<p>The Reformation in Ireland was a movement for the reform of religious life and institutions that was introduced into Ireland by the English administration at the behest of King Henry VIII of England. His desire for an annulment of his marriage was known as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King%27s_Great_Matter" title="King's Great Matter">King's Great Matter</a>. Ultimately <a href="/wiki/Pope_Clement_VII" title="Pope Clement VII">Pope Clement VII</a> refused the petition; consequently it became necessary for the King to assert his lordship over the church in his realm to give legal effect to his wishes. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/English_Parliament" title="English Parliament">English Parliament</a> confirmed the King's supremacy over the Church in the Kingdom of England. This challenge to <a href="/wiki/Papal_supremacy" title="Papal supremacy">Papal supremacy</a> resulted in a breach with the Roman Catholic Church. By 1541, the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Ireland" title="Parliament of Ireland">Irish Parliament</a> had agreed to the change in status of the country from that of a <a href="/wiki/Lordship_of_Ireland" title="Lordship of Ireland">Lordship</a> to that of <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Ireland" title="Kingdom of Ireland">Kingdom of Ireland</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>Unlike similar movements for religious reform on the continent of Europe, the various phases of the English Reformation as it developed in Ireland were largely driven by changes in government policy, to which public opinion in England gradually accommodated itself. However, a number of factors complicated the adoption of the religious innovations in Ireland; the majority of the population there adhered to the Catholic Church. However, in the city of <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin</a> the Reformation took hold under the auspices of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/George_Browne_(Archbishop_of_Dublin)" title="George Browne (Archbishop of Dublin)">George Browne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Archbishop_of_Dublin" title="Archbishop of Dublin">Archbishop of Dublin</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Italy">Italy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reformation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Italy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Reformation_in_Italy" title="Reformation in Italy">Reformation in Italy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Girolamo_Savonarola" title="Girolamo Savonarola">Girolamo Savonarola</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Waldenser-Wappen.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="465" data-file-width="400" decoding="async" height="198" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Waldenser-Wappen.jpg/170px-Waldenser-Wappen.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Waldenser-Wappen.jpg/255px-Waldenser-Wappen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Waldenser-Wappen.jpg/340px-Waldenser-Wappen.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Waldenser-Wappen.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Waldensian symbol <i>Lux lucet in tenebris</i> ("Light glows in the darkness")</div></div></div>
<p>Word of the Protestant reformers reached Italy in the 1520s but never caught on. Its development was stopped by the Counter-Reformation, the Inquisition and also popular disinterest. Not only was the Church highly aggressive in seeking out and suppressing heresy, but there was a shortage of Protestant leadership. No one translated the Bible into Italian; few tracts were written. No core of Protestantism emerged. The few preachers who did take an interest in "Lutheranism", as it was called in Italy, were suppressed or went into exile to northern countries where their message was well received. As a result, the Reformation exerted almost no lasting influence in Italy, except for strengthening the Catholic Church and pushing for an end to ongoing abuses during the Counter-Reformation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McCulloch401_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-McCulloch401-81">[77]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Firp169_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-Firp169-82">[78]</a></sup>
</p><p>Some Protestants left Italy and became outstanding activists of the European Reformation, mainly in the <a href="/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Lithuanian_Commonwealth" title="Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth">Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth</a> (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Giorgio_Biandrata" title="Giorgio Biandrata">Giorgio Biandrata</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bernardino_Ochino" title="Bernardino Ochino">Bernardino Ochino</a>, Giovanni Alciato, Giovanni Battista Cetis, <a href="/wiki/Fausto_Sozzini" title="Fausto Sozzini">Fausto Sozzini</a>, <a href="/wiki/Francesco_Stancaro" title="Francesco Stancaro">Francesco Stancaro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Valentino_Gentile" title="Giovanni Valentino Gentile">Giovanni Valentino Gentile</a>), who propagated <a href="/wiki/Nontrinitarianism" title="Nontrinitarianism">Nontrinitarianism</a> there and were chief instigators of the movement of <a href="/wiki/Polish_Brethren" title="Polish Brethren">Polish Brethren</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Church457_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-Church457-83">[79]</a></sup> Some also fled to England and Switzerland, including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peter_Vermigli" title="Peter Vermigli">Peter Vermigli</a>.
</p><p>In 1532, the <a href="/wiki/Waldensians" title="Waldensians">Waldensians</a>, who had been already present centuries before the Reformation, aligned themselves and adopted the Calvinist theology. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Waldensian_Church" title="Waldensian Church">Waldensian Church</a> survived in the <a href="/wiki/Western_Alps" title="Western Alps">Western Alps</a> through many persecutions and remains a Protestant church in Italy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wald_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wald-84">[80]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="Polish.E2.80.93Lithuanian_Commonwealth"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Polish–Lithuanian_Commonwealth">Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reformation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reformation_in_Poland" title="Reformation in Poland">Reformation in Poland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Counter-Reformation_in_Poland" title="Counter-Reformation in Poland">Counter-Reformation in Poland</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Johannes_a_Lasco.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1166" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="248" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Johannes_a_Lasco.JPG/170px-Johannes_a_Lasco.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Johannes_a_Lasco.JPG/255px-Johannes_a_Lasco.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Johannes_a_Lasco.JPG/340px-Johannes_a_Lasco.JPG 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Johannes_a_Lasco.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Jan_%C5%81aski" title="Jan Łaski">Jan Łaski</a> sought unity between various Christian Churches in the Commonwealth, and participated in the English Reformation.</div></div></div>
<p>In the first half of the 16th century, the enormous <a href="/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Lithuanian_Commonwealth" title="Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth">Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth</a> was a country of many religions and Churches, including: Roman Catholics, Byzantine Orthodox, <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Apostolic_Church" title="Armenian Apostolic Church">Armenian Oriental Orthodox</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ashkenazi_Jews" title="Ashkenazi Jews">Ashkenazi Jews</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Karaites" title="Crimean Karaites">Karaites</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam" title="Sunni Islam">Sunni Muslims</a>. The various groups had their own juridical systems. On the eve of the Protestant Reformation, Christianity held the predominate position within the Kingdom of Poland and the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Lithuania" title="Grand Duchy of Lithuania">Grand Duchy of Lithuania</a>, and Catholicism received preferential treatment at the expense of the Eastern and Oriental Orthodox.
</p><p>The Reformation first entered Poland through the mostly German-speaking areas in the country's north. In the 1520s Luther's reforms spread among the mostly German-speaking inhabitants of such major cities as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Danzig" title="Danzig">Danzig</a> (now <a href="/wiki/Gda%C5%84sk" title="Gdańsk">Gdańsk</a>), <a href="/wiki/Toru%C5%84" title="Toruń">Thorn</a> (now <a href="/wiki/Toru%C5%84" title="Toruń">Toruń</a>) and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Elbing" title="Elbing">Elbing</a> (now <a href="/wiki/Elbl%C4%85g" title="Elbląg">Elbląg</a>). In <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6nigsberg" title="Königsberg">Königsberg</a> (now <a href="/wiki/Kaliningrad" title="Kaliningrad">Kaliningrad</a>), in 1530, a Polish-language edition of <a href="/wiki/Luther%27s_Small_Catechism" title="Luther's Small Catechism">Luther's Small Catechism</a> was published. The <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Prussia" title="Duchy of Prussia">Duchy of Prussia</a>, a vassal of the <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_the_Kingdom_of_Poland" title="Crown of the Kingdom of Poland">Polish Crown</a> ruled by the <a href="/wiki/Teutonic_Order" title="Teutonic Order">Teutonic Knights</a>, emerged as a key center of the movement, with numerous publishing houses issuing not only Bibles, but also catechisms, in German, Polish and Lithuanian. In 1525 the last Grand Master of the Teutonic Knights secularised the territory, became Lutheran, and established Lutheranism as the state church.
</p><p>Lutheranism found few adherents among the other peoples of the two countries. Calvinism became the most numerous Protestant group because Calvin's teachings on the role of the state within religion appealed to the nobility (known as <a href="/wiki/Szlachta" title="Szlachta">szlachta</a>), mainly in <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Poland" title="Lesser Poland">Lesser Poland</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Lithuania" title="Grand Duchy of Lithuania">Grand Duchy of Lithuania</a>. Several publishing houses were opened in Lesser Poland in the mid-16th century in such locations as <a href="/wiki/S%C5%82omniki" title="Słomniki">Słomniki</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rak%C3%B3w,_Kielce_County" title="Raków, Kielce County">Raków</a>. At that time, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mennonite" title="Mennonite">Mennonites</a> and <a href="/wiki/Moravian_Church" title="Moravian Church">Czech Brothers</a> came to Poland. The former settled in the <a href="/wiki/Vistula" title="Vistula">Vistula</a> Delta where they used their agricultural abilities to turn parts of the delta into plodders. The latter settled mostly in <a href="/wiki/Greater_Poland" title="Greater Poland">Greater Poland</a> around <a href="/wiki/Leszno" title="Leszno">Leszno</a>. Later on, Socinus and his followers emigrated to Poland. Originally the Reformed Church in Poland included both the Calvinists and the Anti-trinitarians (also known as the Socinians and the <a href="/wiki/Polish_Brethren" title="Polish Brethren">Polish Brethren</a>); however, they eventually split due to an inability to reconcile their divergent views on the Trinity. Both Catholics and Orthodox Christians converts became Calvinists and the Anti-Trinitarians.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>The Commonwealth was unique in Europe in the 16th century for its widespread tolerance confirmed by the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Confederation" title="Warsaw Confederation">Warsaw Confederation</a>. This agreement granted religious toleration to all nobles: peasants living on nobile estates did not receive the same protections. In 1563, the <a href="/wiki/Brest_Bible" title="Brest Bible">Brest Bible</a> was published (see also <a href="/wiki/Bible_translations_into_Polish" title="Bible translations into Polish">Bible translations into Polish</a>). The period of tolerance came under strain during the reign of King <a href="/wiki/Sigismund_III_Vasa" title="Sigismund III Vasa">Sigismund III Vasa</a> (Zygmunt Wasa). Sigismund, who was also the King of Sweden until deposed, was educated by Jesuits in Sweden before his election as King of the Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth. During his reign, he selected Catholics for the highest offices in the country. This created resentment amongst the Protestant nobility; however, the country did not experience a religiously motivated civil war. Despite concerted efforts, the nobility rejected efforts to revise or rescind the Confederation of Warsaw, and protected this agreement.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Deluge_(history)" title="Deluge (history)">Deluge</a>, a 20-year period of almost continual warfare, marked the turning point in attitudes. During the war with Sweden, when King <a href="/wiki/John_II_Casimir_Vasa" title="John II Casimir Vasa">John Casimir</a> (Jan Kazimierz) fled to <a href="/wiki/Silesia" title="Silesia">Silesia</a>, the Icon of <a href="/wiki/Black_Madonna_of_Cz%C4%99stochowa" title="Black Madonna of Częstochowa">Mary of Częstochowa</a> became the rallying point for military opposition to the Swedish forces. Upon his return to the country Kihn John Casimir crowned <a href="/wiki/The_Most_Holy_Virgin_Mary,_Queen_of_Poland" title="The Most Holy Virgin Mary, Queen of Poland">Mary a Queen of Poland</a>. Despite these wars against Protestant, Orthodox, and Muslim neighbours, the Confederation of Warsaw held with one notable exception. In the aftermath of the Swedish withdrawal and truce, attitudes throughout the nobility (Catholic, Orthodox, and Protestant) turned against the Polish Brethren. In 1658 the Polish Brethren were forced to leave the country. They were permitted to sell their immovable property and take their movable property; however, it is still unknown whether they received fair-market value for their lands. In 1666, the <a href="/wiki/Sejm_of_the_Polish%E2%80%93Lithuanian_Commonwealth" title="Sejm of the Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth">Sejm</a> banned <a href="/wiki/Apostasy" title="Apostasy">apostasy</a> from Catholicism to any other religion, under penalty of death. Finally, in 1717, the <a href="/wiki/Silent_Sejm" title="Silent Sejm">Silent Sejm</a> banned non-Catholics from becoming deputies of the Parliament.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>The strategy the Catholic Church took towards reconverting the Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth differed from its strategy elsewhere. The unique government (Poland was a republic where the citizen nobility owned the state) meant the king could not enforce a religious settlement even he if so desired. Instead the Catholic Church undertook a long and steady campaign of persuasion. In the <a href="/wiki/Ruthenia" title="Ruthenia">Ruthenian</a> lands (predominately modern day <a href="/wiki/Belarus" title="Belarus">Belarus</a> &amp; <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a>) the Orthodox Church also undertook a similar strategy. Additionally, the Orthodox also sought to join the Catholic Church (accomplished in the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_Brest" title="Union of Brest">Union of Brześć</a> [<a href="/wiki/Brest,_Belarus" title="Brest, Belarus">Brest</a>]); however, this union failed to achieve a lasting, permanent, and complete union of the Catholics and Orthodox in the Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth. An important component of the Catholic Reformation in Poland was education. Numerous colleges and universities were set up throughout the country: the Jesuits and <a href="/wiki/Piarists" title="Piarists">Piarists</a> were important in this regard but there were contributions of other religious orders such as the <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Order" title="Dominican Order">Dominicans</a>. While in the middle of the 16th century the nobility mostly sent their sons abroad for education (the new German Protestant universities were important in this regard), by the mid-1600s the nobility mostly stayed home for education. The quality of the new Catholic schools was so great that Protestants willingly sent their children to these schools. Through their education, many nobles became appreciative of Catholicism or out-right converted. Even though the majority of the nobility were Catholic circa 1700, Protestants remained in these lands and pockets of Protestantism could be found outside the German-speaking lands of the former Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth into the 20th century.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>Among the most important Protestants of the Commonwealth were <a href="/wiki/Miko%C5%82aj_Rej" title="Mikołaj Rej">Mikołaj Rej</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marcin_Czechowic" title="Marcin Czechowic">Marcin Czechowic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andrzej_Frycz_Modrzewski" title="Andrzej Frycz Modrzewski">Andrzej Frycz Modrzewski</a> and <a href="/wiki/Symon_Budny" title="Symon Budny">Symon Budny</a>.
</p><p>For more information see the following:
</p>
<ul><li>Kot, Stanislas. <i>Socinianism in Poland: The Social and Political Ideas of the Polish Antitrinitarians in the Sixteenth and Seventeenth Centuries</i>. Translated by Earl Morse Wilbur. Bacon Hill Boston: Starr King Press, 1957.</li>
<li>Tazbir, Janusz. <i>A State without Stakes: Polish Religious Toleration in the Sixteenth and Seventeenth Centuries</i>. Translated by A. T. Jordan. Panstwowy Instytut Wydawniczy, 1973.</li>
<li>Kłoczowski, Jerzy. <i>A History of Polish Christianity. [Dzieje Chrześcijaństwa Polskiego]</i>.English. Cambridge, U.K.; New York: Cambridge University Press, 2000.</li>
<li>Gudziak, Borys A. Crisis and Reform: The Kyivan Metropolitanate, the Patriarchate of Constantinople, and the Genesis of the Union of Brest. Harvard Series in Ukrainian Studies, 2001.</li>
<li>Teter, Magda. Jews and Heretics in Catholic Poland: A Beleaguered Church in the Post-Reformation Era. Cambridge: Cambridge University Press, 2009.</li>
<li>Nowakowska, Natalia. King Sigismund of Poland and Martin Luther: The Reformation before Confessionalization. Oxford, United Kingdom: Oxford University Press, 2018.</li></ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Moldova">Moldova</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reformation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Moldova">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Reformation_and_Counterreformation_in_Moldavia.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2387" data-file-width="3054" decoding="async" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Reformation_and_Counterreformation_in_Moldavia.svg/200px-Reformation_and_Counterreformation_in_Moldavia.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Reformation_and_Counterreformation_in_Moldavia.svg/300px-Reformation_and_Counterreformation_in_Moldavia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Reformation_and_Counterreformation_in_Moldavia.svg/400px-Reformation_and_Counterreformation_in_Moldavia.svg.png 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Reformation_and_Counterreformation_in_Moldavia.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Reformation in Moldova</div></div></div>
<p>The Reformation was very insignificant in what is now <a href="/wiki/Moldova" title="Moldova">Moldova</a> and saw single congregations of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hussitism" title="Hussitism">Hussitism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Calvinism" title="Calvinism">Calvinism</a> being founded across <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Besserabia" title="Besserabia">Besserabia</a>. During the Reformation era, Moldova was repeatedly invaded.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Slovenia">Slovenia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reformation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Slovenia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Slovenia#Protestantism" title="Religion in Slovenia">Religion in Slovenia § Protestantism</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Primoz-Trubar.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3971" data-file-width="2623" decoding="async" height="257" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Primoz-Trubar.jpg/170px-Primoz-Trubar.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Primoz-Trubar.jpg/255px-Primoz-Trubar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Primoz-Trubar.jpg/340px-Primoz-Trubar.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Primoz-Trubar.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Primo%C5%BE_Trubar" title="Primož Trubar">Primož Trubar</a>, a Lutheran reformer in Slovenia</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Primo%C5%BE_Trubar" title="Primož Trubar">Primož Trubar</a> is notable for consolidating the <a href="/wiki/Slovene_language" title="Slovene language">Slovene language</a> and is considered to be the key figure of Slovenian cultural history, in many aspects a major Slovene historical personality.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Voglar_I_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-Voglar_I-85">[81]</a></sup> He was the key figure of the Protestant Church of the <a href="/wiki/Slovene_Lands" title="Slovene Lands">Slovene Lands</a>, as he was its founder and its first superintendent. The first books in Slovene, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catechismus" title="Catechismus">Catechismus</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Abecedarium_(Trubar)" title="Abecedarium (Trubar)">Abecedarium</a></i>, were written by Trubar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[82]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Slovakia">Slovakia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reformation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Slovakia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Reformation_in_the_Kingdom_of_Hungary" title="Reformation in the Kingdom of Hungary">Reformation in the Kingdom of Hungary</a></div>
<p>At one point in history<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (January 2019)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup>, the majority of <a href="/wiki/Slovaks" title="Slovaks">Slovaks</a> (~60%) were <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lutherans" title="Lutherans">Lutherans</a>. <a href="/wiki/Calvinism" title="Calvinism">Calvinism</a> was popular among the Hungarians who inhabited the southernmost parts of what is now Slovakia. Back then, Slovakia used to be a part of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hungary" title="Kingdom of Hungary">Kingdom of Hungary</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Counter-Reformation" title="Counter-Reformation">Counter-Reformation</a> implemented by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Habsburgs" title="Habsburgs">Habsburgs</a> severely damaged Slovakian Protestantism, although in the 2010s Protestants are still a substantial minority (~10%) in the country.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Croatia">Croatia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reformation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Croatia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Lutheranism" title="Lutheranism">Lutheranism</a> reached northern parts of the country.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Serbia">Serbia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reformation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Serbia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Protestantism_in_Serbia" title="Protestantism in Serbia">Protestantism in Serbia</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Vojvodina" title="Vojvodina">Vojvodina</a> turned partially <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lutheran" title="Lutheran">Lutheran</a>.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Greece">Greece</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reformation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Greece">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Orthodoxy_in_Greece_(1453%E2%80%931821)#cite_ref-ZAKYTHINOS108_127-0" title="Timeline of Orthodoxy in Greece (1453–1821)">Timeline of Orthodoxy in Greece (1453–1821) § cite ref-ZAKYTHINOS108 127-0</a></div>
<p>The Protestant teachings of the Western Church were also briefly adopted within the Eastern Orthodox Church through the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greek_people" title="Greek people">Greek</a> <a href="/wiki/Ecumenical_Patriarch_of_Constantinople" title="Ecumenical Patriarch of Constantinople">Patriarch</a> <a href="/wiki/Cyril_Lucaris" title="Cyril Lucaris">Cyril Lucaris</a> in 1629 with the publishing of the <i>Confessio</i> (Calvinistic doctrine) in <a href="/wiki/Geneva" title="Geneva">Geneva</a>. Motivating factors in their decision to adopt aspects of the Reformation included the <a href="/wiki/East%E2%80%93West_Schism" title="East–West Schism">historical rivalry</a> and mistrust between the <a href="/wiki/Greek_Orthodox_Church" title="Greek Orthodox Church">Greek Orthodox</a> and the Roman Catholic Churches along with their concerns of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jesuit" title="Jesuit">Jesuit</a> priests entering Greek lands in their attempts to propagate the teachings of the <a href="/wiki/Counter-Reformation" title="Counter-Reformation">Counter-Reformation</a> to the Greek populace. He subsequently sponsored <a href="/wiki/Maximos_of_Gallipoli" title="Maximos of Gallipoli">Maximos of Gallipoli</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Bible_translations_into_Greek" title="Bible translations into Greek">translation of the New Testament</a> into the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Modern_Greek_language" title="Modern Greek language">Modern Greek language</a> and it was published in Geneva in 1638. Upon Lucaris's death in 1638, the conservative factions within the Eastern Orthodox Church held two synods: the Synod of Constantinople (1638) and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Synod_of_Ia%C8%99i" title="Synod of Iași">Synod of Iași</a> (1642) criticising the reforms and, in the 1672 convocation led by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Patriarch_Dositheos_II_of_Jerusalem" title="Patriarch Dositheos II of Jerusalem">Dositheos</a>, they officially condemned the Calvinistic doctrines.
</p><p>In 2019, <a href="/wiki/Christos_Yannaras" title="Christos Yannaras">Christos Yannaras</a> told <a href="/wiki/Norman_Russell" title="Norman Russell">Norman Russell</a> that although he had participated in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zo%C3%AB_movement" title="Zoë movement">Zoë movement</a>, he had come to regard it as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crypto-Protestant" title="Crypto-Protestant">Crypto-Protestant</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[83]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Ottoman_Empire">Ottoman Empire</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reformation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Ottoman Empire">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Protestantism_in_Turkey" title="Protestantism in Turkey">Protestantism in Turkey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Protestantism_and_Islam#Mutual_tolerance" title="Protestantism and Islam">Protestantism and Islam § Mutual tolerance</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jeremias_II_of_Constantinople#The_Greek_Augsburg_Confession" title="Jeremias II of Constantinople">Jeremias II of Constantinople § The Greek Augsburg Confession</a></div>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Spread">Spread</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reformation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: Spread">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Reformation spread throughout Europe beginning in 1517, reaching its peak between 1545 and 1620. The greatest geographical extent of Protestantism occurred at some point between 1545 and 1620. In 1620, the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_White_Mountain" title="Battle of White Mountain">Battle of White Mountain</a> defeated Protestants in Bohemia (now the Czech Republic) who sought to have the 1609 <a href="/wiki/Letter_of_Majesty" title="Letter of Majesty">Letter of Majesty</a> upheld.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HolyRomanEmpire_1618.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2362" data-file-width="2362" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/HolyRomanEmpire_1618.png/220px-HolyRomanEmpire_1618.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/HolyRomanEmpire_1618.png/330px-HolyRomanEmpire_1618.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/HolyRomanEmpire_1618.png/440px-HolyRomanEmpire_1618.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:HolyRomanEmpire_1618.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Religious fragmentation in Central Europe at the outbreak of the <a href="/wiki/Thirty_Years%27_War" title="Thirty Years' War">Thirty Years' War</a> (1618).</div></div></div>
<p><br/>
</p>
<div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:702px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Protestant_Reformation.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1720" data-file-width="2045" decoding="async" height="589" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/The_Protestant_Reformation.svg/700px-The_Protestant_Reformation.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/The_Protestant_Reformation.svg/1050px-The_Protestant_Reformation.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/The_Protestant_Reformation.svg/1400px-The_Protestant_Reformation.svg.png 2x" width="700"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Protestant_Reformation.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Reformation at its peak, superimposed on modern European borders</div></div></div><p>.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Thirty_Years%27_War" title="Thirty Years' War">Thirty Years' War</a> began in 1618 and brought a drastic territorial and demographic decline when the House of Habsburg introduced counter-reformational measures throughout their vast possessions in Central Europe. Although the <a href="/wiki/Thirty_Years%27_War" title="Thirty Years' War">Thirty Years' War</a> concluded with the <a href="/wiki/Peace_of_Westphalia" title="Peace of Westphalia">Peace of Westphalia</a>, the French <a href="/wiki/Counter-Reformation#Politics" title="Counter-Reformation">Wars of the Counter-Reformation</a> continued, as well as the expulsion of Protestants in Austria.
</p>
<div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:702px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Counterreformation.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1720" data-file-width="2045" decoding="async" height="589" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/The_Counterreformation.svg/700px-The_Counterreformation.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/The_Counterreformation.svg/1050px-The_Counterreformation.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/The_Counterreformation.svg/1400px-The_Counterreformation.svg.png 2x" width="700"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Counterreformation.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Reformation &amp; the Counter-Reformation—both at their end—and superimposed on modern European borders</div></div></div></div><p>According to a 2020 study in the <i>American Sociological Review</i>, the Reformation spread earliest to areas where Luther had pre-existing social relations, such as mail correspondents, and former students, as well as where he had visited. The study argues that these social ties contributed more to the Reformation's early breakthroughs than the printing press.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[84]</a></sup>
</p><h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Conclusion_and_legacy">Conclusion and legacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reformation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: Conclusion and legacy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>There is no universal agreement on the exact or approximate date the Reformation ended. Various interpretations emphasise different dates, entire periods, or argue that the Reformation never really ended.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> However, there are a few popular interpretations. <a href="/wiki/Peace_of_Augsburg" title="Peace of Augsburg">Peace of Augsburg</a> in 1555 officially ended the religious struggle between the two groups and made the legal division of Christianity permanent within the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a>, allowing rulers to choose either <a href="/wiki/Lutheranism" title="Lutheranism">Lutheranism</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism" title="Roman Catholicism">Roman Catholicism</a> as the official <a href="/wiki/Creed" title="Creed">confession</a> of their state. It could be considered to end with the enactment of the <a href="/wiki/Creed#Christian_confessions_of_faith" title="Creed">confessions of faith</a>. Other suggested ending years relate to the <a href="/wiki/Counter-Reformation" title="Counter-Reformation">Counter-Reformation</a> or the 1648 <a href="/wiki/Peace_of_Westphalia" title="Peace of Westphalia">Peace of Westphalia</a>. From a <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic</a> perspective, the <a href="/wiki/Second_Vatican_Council" title="Second Vatican Council">Second Vatican Council</a> called for an end to the Counter-Reformation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[85]</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>In the history of theology or philosophy, the Reformation era ended with the Age of Orthodoxy. The Orthodox Period, also termed the <a href="/wiki/Template:17th-century_scholasticism" title="Template:17th-century scholasticism">Scholastic Period</a>, succeeded the Reformation with the 1545–1563 <i>Council of Trent</i>, the 1562 Anglican <i>Thirty-nine Articles</i>, the 1580 <i>Book of Concord</i>, and other <a href="/wiki/Creed#Christian_confessions_of_faith" title="Creed">confessions of faith</a>. The Orthodox Era ended with the development of both Pietism and the Enlightenment.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Peace_of_Westphalia" title="Peace of Westphalia">Peace of Westphalia</a> might be considered to be the event that ended the Reformation.</li>
<li>Some historians<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too-vague attribution or weasel words. (September 2021)">who?</span></a></i>]</sup> argue that the Reformation never ended as new churches have splintered from the Catholic Church (e.g., Old Catholics, Polish National Catholic Church, etc.), as well as all the various Protestant churches that exist today. No church splintering from the Catholic Church since the 17th century has done so on the basis of the same issues animating the Reformation, however.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li></ul>
<h3><span id="Thirty_Years.27_War:_1618.E2.80.931648"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Thirty_Years'_War:_1618–1648">Thirty Years' War: 1618–1648</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reformation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: Thirty Years' War: 1618–1648">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Westfaelischer_Friede_in_Muenster_(Gerard_Terborch_1648).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4649" data-file-width="6000" decoding="async" height="170" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Westfaelischer_Friede_in_Muenster_%28Gerard_Terborch_1648%29.jpg/220px-Westfaelischer_Friede_in_Muenster_%28Gerard_Terborch_1648%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Westfaelischer_Friede_in_Muenster_%28Gerard_Terborch_1648%29.jpg/330px-Westfaelischer_Friede_in_Muenster_%28Gerard_Terborch_1648%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Westfaelischer_Friede_in_Muenster_%28Gerard_Terborch_1648%29.jpg/440px-Westfaelischer_Friede_in_Muenster_%28Gerard_Terborch_1648%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Westfaelischer_Friede_in_Muenster_(Gerard_Terborch_1648).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Westphalia" title="Treaty of Westphalia">Treaty of Westphalia</a> allowed <a href="/wiki/Calvinism" title="Calvinism">Calvinism</a> to be freely exercised, reducing the need for <a href="/wiki/Crypto-Calvinism" title="Crypto-Calvinism">Crypto-Calvinism</a></div></div></div>
<p>The Reformation and Counter-Reformation era conflicts are termed the <a href="/wiki/European_wars_of_religion" title="European wars of religion">European wars of religion</a>. In particular, the <a href="/wiki/Thirty_Years%27_War" title="Thirty Years' War">Thirty Years' War</a> (1618–1648) devastated much of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Early_Modern_history_of_Germany" title="Early Modern history of Germany">Germany</a>, killing between 25% and 40% of its entire population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[86]</a></sup> The Catholic <a href="/wiki/House_of_Habsburg" title="House of Habsburg">House of Habsburg</a> and its allies fought against the Protestant princes of Germany, supported at various times by Denmark, Sweden and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_France" title="Kingdom of France">France</a>. The Habsburgs, who ruled Spain, Austria, the <a href="/wiki/Lands_of_the_Bohemian_Crown" title="Lands of the Bohemian Crown">Crown of Bohemia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hungary" title="Kingdom of Hungary">Hungary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slovene_Lands" title="Slovene Lands">Slovene Lands</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Netherlands" title="Spanish Netherlands">Spanish Netherlands</a> and much of Germany and Italy, were staunch defenders of the Catholic Church. Some<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too-vague attribution or weasel words. (November 2018)">who?</span></a></i>]</sup> historians believe that the era of the Reformation came to a close when Catholic France allied itself with Protestant states against the Habsburg dynasty.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>Two main tenets of the <a href="/wiki/Peace_of_Westphalia" title="Peace of Westphalia">Peace of Westphalia</a>, which ended the Thirty Years' War, were:
</p>
<ul><li>All parties would now recognise the <a href="/wiki/Peace_of_Augsburg" title="Peace of Augsburg">Peace of Augsburg</a> of 1555, by which each prince would have the right to determine the religion of his own state, the options being Catholicism, Lutheranism, and now Calvinism (the principle of <span title="Latin-language text"><i lang="la"><a href="/wiki/Cuius_regio,_eius_religio" title="Cuius regio, eius religio">cuius regio, eius religio</a></i></span>).</li>
<li>Christians living in principalities where their denomination was <i>not</i> the established church were guaranteed the right to practice their faith in public during allotted hours and in private at their will.</li></ul>
<p>The treaty also effectively ended the Papacy's pan-European political power. <a href="/wiki/Pope_Innocent_X" title="Pope Innocent X">Pope Innocent X</a> declared the treaty "null, void, invalid, iniquitous, unjust, damnable, reprobate, inane, empty of meaning and effect for all times" in his bull <i>Zelo Domus Dei</i>. European sovereigns, Catholic and Protestant alike, ignored his verdict.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ODCCWestphalia_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-ODCCWestphalia-91">[87]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Consequences_of_the_Reformation">Consequences of the Reformation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reformation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: Consequences of the Reformation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Six princes of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a> and rulers of fourteen <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Imperial_Free_City" title="Imperial Free City">Imperial Free Cities</a>, who issued <a href="/wiki/Protestation_at_Speyer" title="Protestation at Speyer">a protest</a> (or dissent) against the edict of the <a href="/wiki/Diet_of_Speyer_(1529)" title="Diet of Speyer (1529)">Diet of Speyer (1529)</a>, were the first individuals to be called Protestants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-etymonline.com_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-etymonline.com-92">[88]</a></sup> The edict reversed concessions made to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lutherans" title="Lutherans">Lutherans</a> with the approval of <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Holy Roman Emperor">Holy Roman Emperor</a> <a href="/wiki/Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles V, Holy Roman Emperor">Charles V</a> <a href="/wiki/Diet_of_Speyer_(1526)" title="Diet of Speyer (1526)">three years earlier</a>. The term <i>protestant</i>, though initially purely political in nature, later acquired a broader sense, referring to a member of any Western church which subscribed to the main Protestant principles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-etymonline.com_92-1"><a href="#cite_note-etymonline.com-92">[88]</a></sup> Today, Protestantism constitutes the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Christian_denominations_by_number_of_members" title="List of Christian denominations by number of members">second-largest form</a> of Christianity (after Catholicism), with a total of 800 million to 1 billion adherents worldwide or about 37% of all Christians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pewforum1_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-pewforum1-93">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gordonconwell.edu_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-gordonconwell.edu-94">[90]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[e]</a></sup> Protestants have developed <a href="/wiki/Protestant_culture" title="Protestant culture">their own culture</a>, with major contributions in education, the humanities and sciences, the political and social order, the economy and the arts and many other fields.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Karl_Heussi_1956_pp._317–319_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-Karl_Heussi_1956_pp._317–319-97">[92]</a></sup> The following outcomes of the Reformation regarding <a href="/wiki/Human_capital" title="Human capital">human capital</a> formation, the <a href="/wiki/Protestant_work_ethic" title="Protestant work ethic">Protestant ethic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Economic_development" title="Economic development">economic development</a>, <a href="/wiki/Governance" title="Governance">governance</a>, and "dark" outcomes have been identified by scholars:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_40-2"><a href="#cite_note-:0-40">[37]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_capital_formation">Human capital formation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reformation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=56" title="Edit section: Human capital formation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul><li>Higher literacy rates.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Becker_531–596_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-Becker_531–596-98">[93]</a></sup></li>
<li>Lower gender gap in school enrollment and literacy rates.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[94]</a></sup></li>
<li>Higher primary school enrollment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[95]</a></sup></li>
<li>Higher public spending on schooling and better educational performance of military conscripts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[96]</a></sup></li>
<li>Higher capability in reading, numeracy, essay writing, and history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[97]</a></sup></li></ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Protestant_ethic">Protestant ethic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reformation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=57" title="Edit section: Protestant ethic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul><li>More hours worked.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[98]</a></sup></li>
<li>Divergent work attitudes of Protestant and Catholics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[99]</a></sup></li>
<li>Fewer referendums on leisure, state intervention, and redistribution in Swiss cantons with more Protestants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[100]</a></sup></li>
<li>Lower life satisfaction when unemployed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[101]</a></sup></li>
<li>Pro-market attitudes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[102]</a></sup></li>
<li>Income differences between Protestants and Catholics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Becker_531–596_98-1"><a href="#cite_note-Becker_531–596-98">[93]</a></sup></li></ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Economic_development">Economic development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reformation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=58" title="Edit section: Economic development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Katharina-v-Bora-1526.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="600" decoding="async" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Katharina-v-Bora-1526.jpg/170px-Katharina-v-Bora-1526.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Katharina-v-Bora-1526.jpg/255px-Katharina-v-Bora-1526.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Katharina-v-Bora-1526.jpg/340px-Katharina-v-Bora-1526.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Katharina-v-Bora-1526.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Katharina_von_Bora" title="Katharina von Bora">Katharina von Bora</a> played a role in shaping social ethics during the Reformation.</div></div></div>
<ul><li>Different levels of income tax revenue per capita, % of labor force in manufacturing and services, and incomes of male elementary school teachers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Becker_531–596_98-2"><a href="#cite_note-Becker_531–596-98">[93]</a></sup></li>
<li>Growth of Protestant cities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[103]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[104]</a></sup></li>
<li>Greater entrepreneurship among religious minorities in Protestant states.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[105]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[106]</a></sup></li>
<li>Different social ethics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[107]</a></sup></li>
<li>Industrialization.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[108]</a></sup></li></ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Governance">Governance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reformation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=59" title="Edit section: Governance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul><li>The Reformation has been credited as a key factor in the development of the state system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[109]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[110]</a></sup></li>
<li>The Reformation has been credited as a key factor in the formation of transnational advocacy movements.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[111]</a></sup></li>
<li>The Reformation impacted the Western legal tradition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[112]</a></sup></li>
<li>Establishment of state churches.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[113]</a></sup></li>
<li>Poor relief and social welfare regimes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[114]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[115]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/James_Madison" title="James Madison">James Madison</a> noted that <a href="/wiki/Martin_Luther" title="Martin Luther">Martin Luther</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Two_kingdoms_doctrine" title="Two kingdoms doctrine">doctrine of the two kingdoms</a> marked the beginning of the modern conception of <a href="/wiki/Separation_of_church_and_state" title="Separation of church and state">separation of church and state</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[116]</a></sup></li>
<li>The Calvinist and Lutheran doctrine of the <a href="/wiki/Lesser_magistrate" title="Lesser magistrate">lesser magistrate</a> contributed to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Resistance_theory_in_the_Early_Modern_period" title="Resistance theory in the Early Modern period">resistance theory in the Early Modern period</a> and was employed in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Declaration_of_Independence" title="United States Declaration of Independence">United States Declaration of Independence</a>.</li>
<li>Reformers such as Calvin promoted <a href="/wiki/Mixed_government" title="Mixed government">mixed government</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Separation_of_powers" title="Separation of powers">separation of powers</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[117]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-123">[118]</a></sup> which governments such as the United States subsequently adopted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[119]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[120]</a></sup></li></ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_outcomes">Other outcomes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reformation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=60" title="Edit section: Other outcomes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul><li>Witch trials became more common in regions or other jurisdictions where Protestants and Catholics contested the religious market.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[121]</a></sup></li>
<li>Christopher J. Probst, in his book <i>Demonizing the Jews: Luther and the Protestant Church in Nazi Germany</i> (2012), shows that a large number of German Protestant clergy and theologians during the Nazi Third Reich used Luther's hostile publications towards the Jews and Judaism to justify at least in part the anti-Semitic policies of the National Socialists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[122]</a></sup></li>
<li>In its decree on <a href="/wiki/Unitatis_redintegratio" title="Unitatis redintegratio">ecumenism</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Second_Vatican_Council" title="Second Vatican Council">Second Vatican Council</a> of Catholic Bishops declared that by contemporary dialogue that, while still holding views as the One, Holy, Catholic, and Apostolic Church, between the churches "all are led to examine their own faithfulness to Christ's will for the Church and accordingly to undertake with vigor the task of renewal and reform" (<i>Unitatis Redintegratio</i>, 4).</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Historiography">Historiography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reformation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=61" title="Edit section: Historiography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Margaret C. Jacob argues that there has been a dramatic shift in the historiography of the Reformation. Until the 1960s, historians focused their attention largely on the great leaders and theologians of the 16th century, especially Luther, Calvin, and Zwingli. Their ideas were studied in depth. However, the rise of the <a href="/wiki/Social_history" title="Social history">new social history</a> in the 1960s led to looking at history from the bottom up, not from the top down. Historians began to concentrate on the values, beliefs and behavior of the people at large. She finds, "in contemporary scholarship, the Reformation is now seen as a vast cultural upheaval, a social and popular movement, textured and rich because of its diversity."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jacob215_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jacob215-128">[123]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_and_art">Music and art</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reformation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=62" title="Edit section: Music and art">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<p><b>Secular music</b>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/English_Madrigal_School" title="English Madrigal School">English Madrigal School</a></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Greensleeves" title="Greensleeves">Greensleeves</a></i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Madrigal#Continental_Europe" title="Madrigal">German madrigals</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moravian_traditional_music#History" title="Moravian traditional music">Moravian traditional music</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Meistersinger" title="Meistersinger">Meistersinger</a></li></ul>
</div>
<p>Partly due to Martin Luther's love for music, music became important in Lutheranism. The study and practice of music was encouraged in Protestant-majority countries. Songs such as the Lutheran hymns or the Calvinist Psalter became tools for the spread of Protestant ideas and beliefs, as well as identity flags. Similar attitudes developed among Catholics, who in turn encouraged the creation and use of music for religious purposes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[124]</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reformation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=64" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1011085734">.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style><div class="reflist reflist-lower-alpha">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-5"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-5">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">For an example of Reformation history in the Radical Reformation Tradition, see <i><a href="/wiki/The_Trail_of_Blood" title="The Trail of Blood">The Trail of Blood</a></i>.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-34"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-34">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In the end, while the Reformation emphasis on Protestants reading the Scriptures was one factor in the development of literacy, the impact of printing itself, the wider availability of printed works at a cheaper price, and the increasing focus on education and learning as key factors in obtaining a lucrative post, were also significant contributory factors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pettegree543_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pettegree543-33">[32]</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-38"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-38">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In the first decade of the Reformation, Luther's message became a movement, and the output of religious pamphlets in Germany was at its height.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PettegreeHall786_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-PettegreeHall786-37">[35]</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-79"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-79">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">See the wikipedia entry on <a href="/wiki/Joanes_Leizarraga" title="Joanes Leizarraga">Joanes Leizarraga</a>, the priest who did the translation. His manuscript is considered to be a cornerstone in Basque literature, and a pioneering attempt towards Basque language standardization.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-96"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-96">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Most current estimates place the world's Protestant population in the range of 800 million to more than 1 billion. For example, author Hans Hillerbrand estimated a total Protestant population of 833,457,000 in 2004,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-books.google.pl_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-books.google.pl-95">[91]</a></sup> while a report by Gordon-Conwell Theological Seminary – 961,961,000 (with inclusion of independents as defined in this article) in mid-2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gordonconwell.edu_94-1"><a href="#cite_note-gordonconwell.edu-94">[90]</a></sup></span>
</li>
